<div id="review_1639324634" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1639324634" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1639324634?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=male-male-romance">male-male-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1639324634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7957278131723560819">Edit: I just reread this because I have the rest of the series and, I know you aren't going to believe this, but I may have been a little too critical of this book. Go ahead, gasp. It's shocking stuff because I never get ultra-picky when I'm reviewing..<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595914076ra/29866542.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Anyway, I realized that maybe these two FBI guys don't have degrees in English Lit, so maybe that was expecting too much from them. Although, I still hold to the fact that they took too long to figure out who the bad-guy was. All the clues were th</span>
  <span id="freeText7957278131723560819" style="display:none">Edit: I just reread this because I have the rest of the series and, I know you aren't going to believe this, but I may have been a little too critical of this book. Go ahead, gasp. It's shocking stuff because I never get ultra-picky when I'm reviewing..<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595914076ra/29866542.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, I realized that maybe these two FBI guys don't have degrees in English Lit, so maybe that was expecting too much from them. Although, I still hold to the fact that they took too long to figure out who the bad-guy was. All the clues were there.<br>So, I enjoyed the reread better than the preread, or as some might say, the read. <br><br>Here's my original crappy review:<br><br>You know when you read a mystery novel, and there is all of this awesome serial killing going on, and you're trying to figure out who the killer is, and you zoom in on one character but it seems too obvious? The "red herring" guy who you know in the end is totally NOT going to be the killer. It would be too lame. Too expected.<br><br>Yeah, that doesn't happen here. The killer is so obvious that you have to wonder how in the world these guys are working for the FBI and can't figure it out when a housewife in Texas fingered him/her in 10 seconds flat.<br><br>I wanted to yell at the book, "Guys! He's right there! Yes, standing on your left side.... No, your other left..... sheesh!"<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463475302i/19120888._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah, so the serial murders were really cool. Especially once they figure out the "theme", but it takes them a hella long time to figure that out. And, then, the murderer. It's like... dude... is this really the best investigating our government is capable of? Cuz, if so, I think our taxes need to be lower. We can't possibly be paying them above minimum wage without being ripped off. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595914076i/29866543._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Along with being a "mystery", this book is also a romance between the two guys. And, frankly, the romance wasn't that believable either. It's not that they couldn't possibly have been attracted to each other, it was that the characters themselves were so unbelievable. They basically became the other one during the time of the story. Their personalities completely changed. If they had fallen for each other, they basically ended up falling for themselves. That's how weird it was. The uptight one becomes the crazy out-of-control one while the zany guy becomes uptight. It was a gay, bloody Freaky Friday. And, seriously, I wasn't a fan of that movie even as a kid. Lame.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463475302ra/19120889.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Yeah, that was great. Not.<br><br>And yet, even with these problems, I still enjoyed the story well enough. I won't be continuing on with the series, but it kept me entertained. Maybe it was all the sex....<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463475302i/19120890.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18442796375766135515">Time for another reread. I need a Ty/Zane fix.<br/><br/>Rereading 10/4/17 - Jewel made me do it.<br/><br/><b>Original review:</b><br/>While the overall series is a 5+++ stars, this first book is objectively 3.5-4 stars. It's very choppy with its POV shifts and in need of a lot of additional editing down, while still being amazingly well-written. I'll never forget my introduction to Ty Grady and Zane Garrett. Sigh. Do you ever wish you could unread a book/series so you could experience it for the first time all over again? It w</span>
  <span id="freeText18442796375766135515" style="display:none">Time for another reread. I need a Ty/Zane fix.<br /><br />Rereading 10/4/17 - Jewel made me do it.<br /><br /><b>Original review:</b><br />While the overall series is a 5+++ stars, this first book is objectively 3.5-4 stars. It's very choppy with its POV shifts and in need of a lot of additional editing down, while still being amazingly well-written. I'll never forget my introduction to Ty Grady and Zane Garrett. Sigh. Do you ever wish you could unread a book/series so you could experience it for the first time all over again? It would be this series for me.<br /><br />For those of you who haven't read this series? This book is a starter. Ty and Zane are introduced to you in this book. Consider the first episode of your favorite TV show. Does that depict all that the rest of the series is made of? I'm guessing no. There's a reason people in the m/m romance world gush over this series. Book 1 is my least favorite of them all. But it's still chocked full of tender moments of discovering each other while filled with action. Jump in! You won't regret it!<br /><br />Awesome BR reread with Jewel in December 2015 - see thread below to follow along as we read it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18442796375766135515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1896117397" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1896117397" />
    <a title="Jan  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20856081-jan"><img alt="Jan  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534851634p2/20856081.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1896117397?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan  " href="/user/show/20856081-jan">Jan  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20856081-jan?shelf=alpha-male">alpha-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20856081-jan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20856081-jan?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20856081-jan?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20856081-jan?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20856081-jan?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1896117397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13184299284849053805">**** 3.75 stars ****<br/><br/>I really liked this but I didn’t love it, not in epic proportions as most of the others anyway.<br/>Here are my thumbs up points: <br/>The characterisation of both MCs.<br/>The mystery which came across very strong. <br/>Action wise it had a steady pace with no boring times.<br/>Chemistry was there, solid.<br/><br/>What held back my 5*? romance x relationship. <br/><br/>When the story started and we met Zane, <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486165252i/21888610.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>we were led to believe that Zane was perfection whereas Ty on the other hand, was a mess. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486163461i/21888461._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Very first wrong impre</span>
  <span id="freeText13184299284849053805" style="display:none">**** 3.75 stars ****<br><br>I really liked this but I didn’t love it, not in epic proportions as most of the others anyway.<br>Here are my thumbs up points: <br>The characterisation of both MCs.<br>The mystery which came across very strong. <br>Action wise it had a steady pace with no boring times.<br>Chemistry was there, solid.<br><br>What held back my 5*? romance x relationship. <br><br>When the story started and we met Zane, <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486165252i/21888610.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>we were led to believe that Zane was perfection whereas Ty on the other hand, was a mess. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486163461i/21888461._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Very first wrong impressions I must say. I guess we were tricked.<br>As the story progresses and Zane’s layers starts to peel off we realize that Zane is not perfect at all. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486163370i/21888447.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Hands down Zane was the most damaged. He lost his wife, a partner at work and he also had addictions to deal with. <br><br>I didn’t like that every time Zane showed a weakness Ty took a step back. It happened when he mentioned his wife, the drinks and the drugs. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486163370i/21888448.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I also wanted to see them going crazy in lust with each other <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486163370i/21888450.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>but they seemed very restrained both emotionally and physically. There were times when I was left disappointed in regarding to this coldness, like when they were apart for 4 months. When they met again, they went to Ty's place, had a shower, they ate some pizza, talked and went to bed, <b>to sleep</b>, folks. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486163370i/21888449.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, excuse me moi, but why they didn’t jump each other bones is beyond my understanding. Think: you don't see your man for 4 months. What are you going to do when you meet humm?? well, I have no idea what you would do, but I know what I would *snort* <br>Ok, he wasn't <b>HIS </b>man. Still, it frustrated me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486164244i/21888523.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486164850i/21888562.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh! Another thing that I liked A LOT was that the guys didn’t seem to grab where they stood emotionally. AND <b>that</b> made the story believable. I would have hated if it would have turned in instalove. They hated each other at first and in a matter of days they started to feel protective about each other. They were very confused about these feelings. I think this was played very well by the author with their inner monologues. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486164244i/21888524.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall it was a really great read and I am very curious to see what book #2 will bring romance wise.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486165485i/21888620.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sorry I went a bit OTT with the pics but how could I not get excited about Ty &amp; Zane?<br>So damn hot!<br>A pity that I could not show them in full, a serial flagger could be around. <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465253084ra/19330665.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This review has been posted at <a href="https://dirtybooksobsessiongroup.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Dirty Books Obsession</a></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1290556754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6596955110805872699"><b>4.5 Stars!</b><br/><br/>Well....seeing as I am damn near the last person on the planet to read this series I won't fuss too much over a review. <br/><br/>I've been hesitant to read this series based on the number of books. I tend to lose interest, but after reading the spin-off I really wanted to give it a try. I forgot how much I love romantic suspense. Probably because I never seem to figure out the bad guy until the very end. Though I will say I pegged this one early on...but it was never confirmed until the very en</span>
  <span id="freeText6596955110805872699" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars!</b><br /><br />Well....seeing as I am damn near the last person on the planet to read this series I won't fuss too much over a review. <br /><br />I've been hesitant to read this series based on the number of books. I tend to lose interest, but after reading the spin-off I really wanted to give it a try. I forgot how much I love romantic suspense. Probably because I never seem to figure out the bad guy until the very end. Though I will say I pegged this one early on...but it was never confirmed until the very end.<br /><br />Yes, there were things I didn't love. This book was LONG! And the chapters were LONG! Two things I am not a fan of. Not to mention, Ty and Zane also aren't really a couple at all in this book. So the romance aspect is rather limited. <br /><br />But I liked both characters. I loved their banter between each other. I loved the sexual tension. And I really loved when they gave in to that tension. <br /><br />They've both got....issues. But at the same time they have a connection. I am definitely curious to see their relationship develop. <br /><br />Overall a solid start to the series. <br /></span>

I struggled to find the emotion needed; I thought I would feel something once Ty and Zane at least shared a kiss, but nope, didn't </span>
  <span id="freeText8192260497491845207" style="display:none">I'm abandoning this book. Forever. <br /><br />I didn't know what was wrong with it but I couldn't get into the story. It felt dragging on and on. I had books that were longer or more complicated but this one, I couldn't feel any sympathy or feeling for the characters at all. So no, not planning to read the sequel either. No matter how great the series seem to be for other reviewers.<br /> </span>

<div id="review_793510135" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793510135" />
    <a title="Shurrn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22115857-shurrn"><img alt="Shurrn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410564134p2/22115857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/793510135?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shurrn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shurrn" href="/user/show/22115857-shurrn">Shurrn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=romance-modern">romance-modern</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=genre-thriller">genre-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=i-lol-moments">i-lol-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=romance-suspense">romance-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=c-playing-detective">c-playing-detective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=romance-mm">romance-mm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=c-favorite-males">c-favorite-males</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=genre-crime-or-mystery">genre-crime-or-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=i-lgbt">i-lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=series-unfinished">series-unfinished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793510135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9622135190312366574"><b>A genre-crossing thrill ride. Gripping, entertaining, and intriguing.<br/>The perfect launch of a series.</b> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394995715ra/8933272.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>(all spoilers are hidden) <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I’m flattered. I’ve moved up from idiot to moron,” Zane said. “And you have moved up from utterly reprehensible asshole to only moderately annoying asshole.”<br/>“Only?” Ty repeated with a huff. “It takes effort to be this abrasive, I hope you realize.”<br/>“Yeah, I guess so. But you just make it look so easy.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> Serial Killers,<br/>Explosions, <br/>Car Chases,<br/>Gruesome Murders,<br/>A </span>
  <span id="freeText9622135190312366574" style="display:none"><b>A genre-crossing thrill ride. Gripping, entertaining, and intriguing.<br>The perfect launch of a series.</b> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394995715ra/8933272.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(all spoilers are hidden) <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I’m flattered. I’ve moved up from idiot to moron,” Zane said. “And you have moved up from utterly reprehensible asshole to only moderately annoying asshole.”<br>“Only?” Ty repeated with a huff. “It takes effort to be this abrasive, I hope you realize.”<br>“Yeah, I guess so. But you just make it look so easy.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> Serial Killers,<br>Explosions, <br>Car Chases,<br>Gruesome Murders,<br>A literal Love/Hate Relationship...<br><br><b>TY GRADY</b><br>FBI Special Agent<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396280651i/9109990._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Former Marine - Force Recon <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Ty Grady was a rude, insufferable, egotistical, stinking son of a bitch, and Zane was going to need to figure out how to tune him out. Otherwise, he just might give in to the pressure and kill the bastard, for the good of humanity.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>ZANE Z. GARRETT</b><br>FBI Special Agent<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396280927i/9110012._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Former Cyber Division Investigator <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“So here I am; widower, alcoholic, addict, all-around asshole turned squeaky clean by force of will, threat of jail, and sheer terror. I suppose it’s no wonder your ‘pansy ass’ comments get in my craw,”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>There is no way I'm going to have enough time to hit on all of the fantastic qualities of this book, so I'll have to pick out a few...<br><br><b>Character Development:</b> Rarely have I seen the level of character construction and believable development out of two MCs. Especially from a book which clocks in at under 350 pages. Each character fit snugly into their "good cop, bad cop" trope at the beginning, and these two <i>HATE</i> each other from the moment they meet. The idea that they could become effective partners, let alone have a romantic relationship seemed absurd. It was a pleasure to see each of them grow.<br><br>I loved the banter between these two characters. The contrast between the hard-ass jabs and growing tenderness was amazing. I was touched, and immediately found myself hoping they could find a balance which could keep them together. It was obvious that they complimented each other, and needed the support of the other... And the sexy times? Damn. You can't pack that much macho-alpha-male-chip-on-your-shoulder sexual tension into a partnership and NOT wind up with combustible sex...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/459789.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Should I go back to my room tonight?” Ty asked out of the blue. “Or will we be able to work together and fuck each other senseless at the same time?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> Yes, the relationship between Ty and Zane was a major draw for this book, but it wasn't the only focus. After all, the FBI Agents had a job to do, and the focus on catching a serial killer was driving the plot.<br><br><b>There was a cinematic quality to the writing in this book.</b><br>The authors were not describing the settings ad nauseam, but I was always acutely aware of the atmosphere. I mention this because the reader is attempting to solve this crime right along with the heroes, so we are searching for clues and motive in every chapter.<br><br><b>SPEAKING OF WHICH:<br><br>Personal Preference:</b> When I'm reading a crime or mystery novel, I will always get more enjoyment out of the book if I can figure out "who done it" before the big reveal. <i>(It makes me feel smart, and I like to feel that way. Not going to lie; that's just how it is.)</i> However, I do not like for the solution to be so obvious that I start to question the MC's intelligence for not being smart enough to figure out what's going on. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5199022.Cut___Run__Cut___Run___1_" title="Cut &amp; Run (Cut &amp; Run, #1) by Abigail Roux" rel="nofollow noopener">Cut &amp; Run</a> had the perfect balance of a complex case and intelligent investigators. It keeps you on the edge of your seat. Everyone is a suspect.<br><br><b>The Motive:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>I was really impressed at the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe" title="Edgar Allan Poe" rel="nofollow noopener">Edgar Allan Poe</a> method behind the killer's madness. Staging his murders to in an homage to Poe stories had an elegance which proved that the Killer was intelligent. For some reason a crazy person isn't nearly as terrifying as a calculating and smart one.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394992346ra/8933029.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>The Culperate:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>It was obvious from the beginning that the killer must be involved with law enforcement in some capacity. I pegged Tim Henninger as the serial killer when the computer bomb detonated. And while he remained my primary suspect for he rest of the book, there were enough curve balls and red herrings scattered throughout the story to keep me second-guessing my choice. As a matter of fact, I wasn't positive that Henninger was the killer until he shot Agents Ross &amp; Sears.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380381663ra/739051.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>The Climax:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394992346i/8933030.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Perfection. The climax was the culmination of everything awesome in this book. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/261240.The_Cask_of_Amontillado" title="The Cask of Amontillado by Edgar Allan Poe" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cask of Amontillado</a> was the perfect platform for killing Ty. <br>It preyed on Ty's fear of dying slowly in a claustrophobic dark place.<br>It caused Zane to face his worst fear of being separated and unable to save someone he loves...<br><br>That being said, I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/206172.The_Pit_and_the_Pendulum" title="The Pit and the Pendulum by Edgar Allan Poe" rel="nofollow noopener">The Pit and the Pendulum</a> would be the worst way to go for me...<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I'm sure that there are a million other little things which made this book such an enjoyable read, but I'm going to leave off here. It was a great story, I hope you'll read it and love it as much as I did.<br><br><b>
  <u>Some of My Favorite Moments:</u>
</b><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>“Grady, you’re staying in Criminal until you get your ass killed or do something so illegal even <i>I</i> can’t cover for you, understand? Garrett, you’re to make certain he doesn’t do either of those things. Is that clear? And you will both <i>like</i> it.”<br><br>Ty Grady was a rude, insufferable, egotistical, stinking son of a bitch, and Zane was going to need to figure out how to tune him out. Otherwise, he just might give in to the pressure and kill the bastard, for the good of humanity.<br><br>"...I swear to God, if you get me shot, I’ll kill you.”<br><br>“I think you decide what a perfectly polite person would do and then do the absolute opposite. It’s like it’s your life’s goal to be the Antichrist.”<br><br>Zane supposed he should feel all warm and fuzzy about Ty at least not wanting him gruesomely murdered and left to bleed out in his shower or something. Somehow, the sentiment didn’t really inspire much camaraderie, though.<br><br>“Anyone who could be so insubordinate could only have been the total opposite at some point in time,”<br><br>“The threat of castration, unemployment, and hard jail time made me rethink things,” Zane supplied.<br><br>“Are you getting hysterical?” Ty asked eagerly. “Can I smack you?”<br><br>Zane wondered if he coordinated his outfits to look like a slob or if he just really was one.<br><br>“So here I am; widower, alcoholic, addict, all-around asshole turned squeaky clean by force of will, threat of jail, and sheer terror. I suppose it’s no wonder your ‘pansy ass’ comments get in my craw,” Zane muttered.<br><br>“Just don’t get your prissy ass hurt again.”<br>“Better watch it, Grady, I might get to thinking you’re taking a liking to my prissy ass,” Zane said, sliding the gun under the pillow.<br>“I’m sure I’d like parts of it,” Ty shot back as he headed for the door.<br><br>“I’m flattered. I’ve moved up from idiot to moron,” Zane said. “And you have moved up from utterly reprehensible asshole to only moderately annoying asshole.”<br>“Only?” Ty repeated with a huff. “It takes effort to be this abrasive, I hope you realize.”<br>“Yeah, I guess so. But you just make it look so easy.”<br><br>He wore a mask, just like Zane did. It was somehow reassuring.<br><br>Oh, this was going to be an absolute fucking mess, he just knew it.<br><br>Ty grabbed him and pulled him off the counter to kiss him again, forcing himself not to think about the consequences. If he thought about it, he’d cut and run—as far and as fast as he possibly could.<br><br>He couldn’t decide if he was angry or just really fucking turned on. Either way, it was all Zane fucking Garrett’s fault….<br><br>Fuck it. He had never followed the rules anyway.<br><br>“You’re stunning when you’re angry, you little fuck,”<br><br>He couldn’t fuck someone without a sense of humor. It just didn’t sit right with him.<br><br>“Should I go back to my room tonight?” Ty asked out of the blue. “Or will we be able to work together and fuck each other senseless at the same time?”<br><br>Zane was starting to piss him off again. Which was good, he supposed. It meant the urge to lick him all over was passing, at least.<br><br>“Ty, I mean it. Do not go to sleep,” he said firmly.<br>“Nap Nazi,” Ty accused miserably.<br>[...]<br>“Don’t you go to sleep on me. I mean it. I’ll do evil and dastardly things to your body if you do.”<br><br>“Go fuck yourself,” [...] <br>“I’m not that flexible,” Zane muttered.<br><br>Zane shook his head. “Are you feeling this too?” he rasped. This insane, blown-away pleasure, the near impossible-to-assuage hunger, the ache deep inside, contrasted by short moments of tenderness that seemed so out of place. Zane certainly wasn’t sure where they came from, but oh, God….<br>Ty watched him, still trying to slow his breathing and holding him at arm’s distance. “No,” he lied blithely.<br><br>“If you turn out to be the killer I’m going to be all kinds of pissed off, got it?” he warned.<br>Zane threw back his head and laughed. “I got plans for a lot more fucking before any mercy killing, man,”<br><br>“I can’t concentrate on anything, not when all I can think about is you..."<br><br>“You said I wouldn’t miss you.” He drew in a long breath, and his voice was even quieter when he spoke again. “You were wrong.”<br><br>"Even I can’t dodge two bullets at once.”<br>Ty tutted and shook his head sadly. “Not the man I thought you were, then.”<br><br>“You know, you keep turning into a worse and worse idea.”<br><br>Ty had asked; Zane would go for broke. “So,” he murmured. “Is this one addiction I can indulge?”<br><br>“Yeah, well, if you weren’t such a dick…,” Ty murmured with a small smile.<br>Zane snickered. “Works out well since you’re an asshole.”<br>"We’re gonna have to talk about these puns.”<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>
  <u>My Other Reviews in the Cut &amp; Run Series:</u>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer505001142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15123637554890449917">I hate adding books to my <i>everyone-liked-but-me</i> shelf, believe me. It was my second try to read it actually: it couldn’t engage me for the first time, and I thought I just was not in the mood, so I put it aside. For the second time, it was still boring. But I didn’t give up and tried to find those amazing qualities the positive reviews mention. Sadly, with no avail.<br/><br/>Both Ty and Zane irritated me, and the jumping viewpoint made them indistinguishable.<br/><br/>The continuous banter tired me, the suspense bo</span>
  <span id="freeText15123637554890449917" style="display:none">I hate adding books to my <i>everyone-liked-but-me</i> shelf, believe me. It was my second try to read it actually: it couldn’t engage me for the first time, and I thought I just was not in the mood, so I put it aside. For the second time, it was still boring. But I didn’t give up and tried to find those amazing qualities the positive reviews mention. Sadly, with no avail.<br /><br />Both Ty and Zane irritated me, and the jumping viewpoint made them indistinguishable.<br /><br />The continuous banter tired me, the suspense bored me to death, I felt the chemistry forced.<br /><br />Romance – what romance?<br /><br />Poor writing, full of repetitions: heads were cocked 31 times, eyebrows were raised 40 times, eyebrows climbed in surprise twice!, heads were tilted 25 times, and eyes were narrowed 47 times. And there was a glorious moment when two of these were in the same sentence: <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Wait wait, let me guess,” Ty said as he held out his hand toward Zane. “Psychology major with a...,” he narrowed his eyes and cocked his head, “political science minor,” he guessed.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Anyway, it was a disappointment. I have no interest in the following books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15123637554890449917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1360498501456329636" style="display:none">I have never before read a M/M romance book that wasn't about the difficulties of coming out or homophobia or pushing some kind of message. This is the first I have picked up with the intention of finding something entertaining and sexy - and, to be honest, I was completely unsure whether M/M sexytimes was going to turn me on. You're injured! Let's remove your shirt so I can tend to your sexy wounds!"</i>. But I was bored by them. Plus, Ty Grady is a dickwad.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1285851761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8183783772620914235"><i>“Not everything needs to be planned. Not everything needs a why or how.”</i><br/><br/>I've been eyeing this book for years now but never got around to reading it. The <i>Cut & Run</i> series is probably one of the most popular and highest rated series in the m/m category. I had high expectations and wasn't disappointed, but there's still a few things that could've been done better.<br/><br/>First of all the ever changing POV is not my favourite. With two main characters it's perfectly fine to show both sides, but instead of c</span>
  <span id="freeText8183783772620914235" style="display:none"><i>“Not everything needs to be planned. Not everything needs a why or how.”</i><br /><br />I've been eyeing this book for years now but never got around to reading it. The <i>Cut &amp; Run</i> series is probably one of the most popular and highest rated series in the m/m category. I had high expectations and wasn't disappointed, but there's still a few things that could've been done better.<br /><br />First of all the ever changing POV is not my favourite. With two main characters it's perfectly fine to show both sides, but instead of changing the POV chapter by chapter it was more of a paragraph thing. And that was really annoying.<br />Secondly, this is a crime novel, meaning lots of investigating, but I don't think I've ever read a sloppier crime story. The police work put into the case was ridiculous, the case was an easy one to solve, especially because our main characters are two super hardcore men with lots of experience in multiple fields of expertise. It was rather unrealistic, especially the body count.<br /><br />The good thing however was the love-hate relationship and the slow burning romance. I live for that shit. Can't wait to read more of it.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2469353430?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2018</a>

        rated it

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/12460152-cut-run">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=boys-who-like-boys">boys-who-like-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2469353430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4824305617230789530">This narrator is so wooden he gives wood a bad name.<br/><br/>Wait, that didn't come out right...<br/><br/>But I'll say this, there was a sex scene towards the end that he mailed in so hard it had me snorting. For all intents and purposes he yada yada'd it!<br/><br/><i>
  <b>Kissing yada yada... groping yada yada... manhandling yada yada yada... lube yada yada... stretching yada yada... YADA YADA YADA YADA YADA COOOOOMMMMIIIIIINNNNNNGGGGGG!!!<br/><br/>-scene</b>
</i><br/><br/>I cracked up. It was so bad it was comical and that coupled with the fact that I ha</span>
  <span id="freeText4824305617230789530" style="display:none">This narrator is so wooden he gives wood a bad name.<br /><br />Wait, that didn't come out right...<br /><br />But I'll say this, there was a sex scene towards the end that he mailed in so hard it had me snorting. For all intents and purposes he yada yada'd it!<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Kissing yada yada... groping yada yada... manhandling yada yada yada... lube yada yada... stretching yada yada... YADA YADA YADA YADA YADA COOOOOMMMMIIIIIINNNNNNGGGGGG!!!<br /><br />-scene</b>
</i><br /><br />I cracked up. It was so bad it was comical and that coupled with the fact that I have endured worse narrators leads me to give the audio portion of this book <b>2 stars</b>.<br /><br />The mystery/thriller aspect I still find engaging even though I think it's pretty obvious who the killer is. Regardless, I liked the pacing of it and how it unfolded.<br /><br />What I had forgotten was how poorly this story is edited. Truly atrocious editing. Did anyone edit it? If so, I think they might need to go back to editing school for a couple refresher courses.<br /><br />I'd also forgotten how hardheaded and stubborn these two were and how many boneheaded decisions they make. They truly are two teens masquerading as men. Some of the stunts they pulled had me shaking my head AND face palming. The problem is I like these two dingalings. A lot. They make a great team when they're not being idiots.<br /><br />The violence that exists between them really unsettled me this time around. The fight in the alley wasn't so bad but when Ty backhanded Zane... that went all over me. There should never be a time when violence is used against someone you care about in my opinion. But I think there is an aspect of foreplay to it, as fucked up as that is, which leaves me feeling conflicted.<br /><br />As much as I abhor the violence between them, they have phenomenal chemistry and banter. And two characters who can shine through the most woodenest narration known to man has to be recognized, so I'm going to give the story <b>3.5 stars</b>.<br /><br />So <b>2.75 stars total</b> that I'll round up and I will not be recommending the audible version of this to anyone unless you have some fairly severe insomnia and <b>REALLY, and I do mean really</b> need a sedative. <br /></span>

    <a title="Meags" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8542123-meags"><img alt="Meags" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524277146p2/8542123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1022262909?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meags" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meags" href="/user/show/8542123-meags">Meags</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=mm">mm</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=fave-characters">fave-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=survival">survival</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=crime-mystery-suspense">crime-mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=bi-ofy-gfy">bi-ofy-gfy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=panties-just-went-poof">panties-just-went-poof</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1022262909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2096878220003546129"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Seems to me that everyone and their dog has read this book and loved it (the majority, at least), so there isn’t much for me to add. <br/><br/>I really like Ty and Zane, individually and together. I love how messed up both of them are, as demented as that sounds; it gives them somewhere to go as characters, partners <i>and</i> lovers, which I greatly look forward to exploring further throughout the series. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Although, if either guy sleeps with one more random person in future books, I will </span></span>
  <span id="freeText2096878220003546129" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Seems to me that everyone and their dog has read this book and loved it (the majority, at least), so there isn’t much for me to add. <br /><br />I really like Ty and Zane, individually and together. I love how messed up both of them are, as demented as that sounds; it gives them somewhere to go as characters, partners <i>and</i> lovers, which I greatly look forward to exploring further throughout the series. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Although, if either guy sleeps with one more random person in future books, I will call it a day. I <u>hatehatehate</u> when book couples sleep with other people, <i>after</i> they’ve already been together, and they're ‘apparently’ crazy for only each other. You just don’t do that! What, you can’t keep your dick in your pants during one or two short separations?! Ugh. Clearly, I have strong feelings about this and it bugged me immensely in this story. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I found the mystery portion of this story fairly predictable. I called it at around the 30% mark, and therefore, I became increasingly frustrated at the characters for not cracking the case sooner than they did. I also wasn’t a huge fan of the perspective changes, particularly when it transpired mid-paragraph, which it often did. I guess I became use to it at some point, but I still didn’t appreciate it. <br /><br />Overall, it was a great read; an epic crime solving adventure, featuring two strong-willed, slightly broken alpha males who are crazy about each other...what's not to like?<br /><br />******************<br /><br /><b>Re-read: November, 2017</b><br /><br />With a nudge in the right direction by a new friend, now seemed like the right time to begin a second read through of this adored series. Generally, I'm not a huge re-reader - I often worry that my initial reactions will change negatively in some way - but I find myself thinking about this series and these men so often and with such fondness, that I just had to throw caution to the wind and go back to the beginning to experience their journey all over again. <br /><br />Thankfully, I wasn't disappointed. Ty and Zane are <i>still</i> my favourite M/M couple. If anything, I love them more now than ever! Re-reading their first story again, knowing all that comes after, simply made every moment all the more special.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2096878220003546129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_207763678" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207763678" />
    <a title="Nancy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/763271-nancy"><img alt="Nancy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435597527p2/763271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/207763678?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy" href="/user/show/763271-nancy">Nancy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5199023-cut-run">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=shelf-inflicted">shelf-inflicted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=erotic-romance">erotic-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=kindle-borrowed">kindle-borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=march-challenge">march-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=outlaw-reviews">outlaw-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207763678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14237945875346686832"><b>Cross-posted at <a href='http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2017/04/cut-run.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shelf Inflicted</a> and at <a href='http://reviews.logophilos.net/index.php/2017/05/cut-run-by-madeleine-urban-and-abigail-roux/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Outlaw Reviews</a> </b><br/><br/>There was so much wrong with this book: the writing style (switching POVs within the same chapter), the dialogues that felt off, the feats of strength performed with serious injuries, the unbelievable scenarios that had me shaking my head at times. The sole purpose for women in this story were to be killed or to be used as a sperm receptacle. <br/><br/>If poor writing drives you nuts, give this one a pass. Do not read this if you enjoy clever mysteries</span>
  <span id="freeText14237945875346686832" style="display:none"><b>Cross-posted at <a href="http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2017/04/cut-run.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelf Inflicted</a> and at <a href="http://reviews.logophilos.net/index.php/2017/05/cut-run-by-madeleine-urban-and-abigail-roux/" rel="nofollow noopener">Outlaw Reviews</a> </b><br /><br />There was so much wrong with this book: the writing style (switching POVs within the same chapter), the dialogues that felt off, the feats of strength performed with serious injuries, the unbelievable scenarios that had me shaking my head at times. The sole purpose for women in this story were to be killed or to be used as a sperm receptacle. <br /><br />If poor writing drives you nuts, give this one a pass. Do not read this if you enjoy clever mysteries, efficient police work and effective investigations. Sloppy detective work abounds, and the FBI are made to look like a bunch of bumbling incompetents. I figured out the villain in no time at all, and you will too. The villian’s methods and twisted mind, however, captured my interest and I enjoyed the incorporation of classic stories. <br /><br />Despite these egregious flaws, I gobbled up this story like it was the last meal before execution. It was funny, sexy and suspenseful. I loved the prickly Ty and Zane, their anger, fights, their inability to communicate, and their swoon-worthy sharing of feelings. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>““You said I wouldn’t miss you.” He drew in a long breath, and his voice was even quieter when he spoke again. “You were wrong.””<br /><br />“I can’t concentrate on anything, not when all I can think about is you.”</blockquote>
</i><br />On to the next book!<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/16723983-lisa" rel="nofollow noopener">Lisa</a> from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/49647-bookie-nookie-s-erotic-lending-group" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookie Nookie's Erotic Lending Group</a> for lending this to me.</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14237945875346686832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_193727248" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193727248" />
    <a title="Heather C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3103725-heather-c"><img alt="Heather C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367464812p2/3103725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/193727248?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather C" href="/user/show/3103725-heather-c">Heather C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781935192244" href="/book/show/6123653-cut-run">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3103725-heather-c?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3103725-heather-c?shelf=cloud">cloud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3103725-heather-c?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3103725-heather-c?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3103725-heather-c?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3103725-heather-c?shelf=sex-after-40-percent">sex-after-40-percent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3103725-heather-c?shelf=review-on-amazon">review-on-amazon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3103725-heather-c?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3103725-heather-c?shelf=lots-of-tension">lots-of-tension</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3103725-heather-c?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193727248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17272666894624372360"><b>Yes, yes I finally broke down and read this!</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Positives:</u>
</b><br/>♦ The MCs<br/>♦ The mystery<br/>♦ The intensity <br/>♦ The name calling<br/>♦ The banter<br/>♦ The snark<br/>♦ The fighting<br/>♦ The sexual tension<br/>♦ The violent kissing<br/>♦ The angry fucking<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Negatives:</u>
</b><br/>♦ The head hopping!! It was exhausting trying to decipher who was saying, doing, thinking what.  I found myself rereading <i>a lot</i>.<br/>♦ The beginning of the book! It was slow reading for a while. Add in the head hopping and it seemed like it took forever for anything to happen. Bu</span>
  <span id="freeText17272666894624372360" style="display:none"><b>Yes, yes I finally broke down and read this!</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Positives:</u>
</b><br />♦ The MCs<br />♦ The mystery<br />♦ The intensity <br />♦ The name calling<br />♦ The banter<br />♦ The snark<br />♦ The fighting<br />♦ The sexual tension<br />♦ The violent kissing<br />♦ The angry fucking<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Negatives:</u>
</b><br />♦ The head hopping!! It was exhausting trying to decipher who was saying, doing, thinking what.  I found myself rereading <i>a lot</i>.<br />♦ The beginning of the book! It was slow reading for a while. Add in the head hopping and it seemed like it took forever for anything to happen. But about midway it evened out a bit and seemed to move faster. <br />♦ The fighting! I know I listed it above in the "Positives" list but it was sometimes exhausting. Add in the head hopping and I was thoroughly confused.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>What The Fuck?! Are You Serious?!</u>
</b><br />♦ In the first half of the book, Ty and Zane kept saying how it was too dangerous for them to be separated, that they must stick together at all times, yet they left each other multiple times when it was convenient for the story. It didn't make sense to me. <br />♦ The huge time jump in the middle of the book broke the pace of the story for me. It seemed like it was at the point of a major climax...then BAM, 4 months later. Yeah, I know it was important to the story but I felt like something important was missing. <br />♦ Ty and Zane's personality transplants threw me off. I understood the cause and reason behind it, but by the end of the book I was unable to see who the <i>real</i> Ty and who the <i>real</i> Zane were. I hope this comes across more clearly in the next books. <br /><br /><b>I really love Ty <i>and</i> Zane. Sometimes I loved Ty more; other times Zane stole my heart.</b> The are both really fucked up, complex characters that I totally connected with!<br /><br />In the end, I really loved this book, but the exhausting parts were a few too numerous for me to forgive. Surprisingly, I am looking forward to reading the sequel...which is <i>really</i> rare for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17272666894624372360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TewoZ9S8WmZ50jKRw2Dq9Q8bR02MmdugapmcCPYNl0W3ydqfUY+rhfAlyT09K7S1H+j2FkLjzPTVJKrDeqVhiQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZyOFqAqq6BgQjKKTcsMIz9ZO3lrmlblClFV9yY6NpJmdBndQj5kZ+5l7WT+MiFaPxr1vASjvrhYr6EsCAiVSVQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5011368747758229191">Madeleine Urban is a down-home Kentucky girl who’s been writing since she could hold a crayon. Although she has written and published on her own, she truly excels when writing with co-authors. She lives with her husband, who is very supportive of her work, and two canine kids who only allow her to hug them when she has food. She wants to live at Disney World, the home of fairy dust, because she be</span>
  <span id="freeText5011368747758229191" style="display:none">Madeleine Urban is a down-home Kentucky girl who’s been writing since she could hold a crayon. Although she has written and published on her own, she truly excels when writing with co-authors. She lives with her husband, who is very supportive of her work, and two canine kids who only allow her to hug them when she has food. She wants to live at Disney World, the home of fairy dust, because she believes that with hard work, a little luck, and beloved family and friends, dreams really can come true.<br /><br />Visit Madeleine's blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://madeleineurban.livejournal.com/">http://madeleineurban.livejournal.com/</a>. You can contact her at mrs.madeleine.urban@gmail.com.<br />Listen to Madeleine interviewed by Peter Godbold on the Strictly Confidential Radio Show<br /><br />MADELEINE URBAN RETIRED<br />Nov. 17, 2011 - I have made the personal decision to stop writing, for reasons that are important to me, including focusing on my family and my health. Writing and publishing comes with a whole set of expectations and pressures, and I find that it's just too much. While I am sad that this will upset and/or even anger readers, this is the right decision for me.<br /><br />Abigail Roux will be continuing the Ty and Zane series, and I know she'll do a great job. </span>
